               \n                    Tom Murphy                \n            \n                                    During its relatively short existence, Purity Ring has quietly exerted an influence on contemporary pop music. Corin Roddick and Megan James had been musicians in Born Gold when the former started experimenting with beatmaking on tour. That solo effort evolved into a full-blown project after Roddick asked James to sing on an early track. Purity Ring combined bits of the new jack swing-style production popularized by Janet Jackson in the early ’90s with the more accessible end of witch house for a sound that has become the backbone for much of modern mainstream pop: Think the rhythm-rich, breezy yet deep melodies of Lorde and Lady Gaga.
